Rulings on Missed Dhikr and Head Cover During Prayer
This passage lists established rulings (rasm) for muftis regarding dhikr, head cover, and prayer on wudu towel.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on when a missed dhikr is not compensated and the permissibility of praying with uncovered head, and apply these rules to fatwa scenarios.

Core Idea
Missed dhikr in its proper place is not made up; praying head-uncovered is not disliked; it is preferred to avoid praying on a wudu towel.

This lesson covers three distinct rasm rulings from the Ashbah: the treatment of dhikr omitted in its appointed time, the ruling on covering the head during prayer, and the etiquette regarding the wudu towel. These are essential for a mufti to answer everyday questions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of missed dhikr
Determine if the dhikr has a specific place (e.g., tasmi' after rising from bowing). If the place is past, it is not revived.
2
Apply the ruling to head covering
The text states that praying with head uncovered is not disliked (la yukrah). This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.
3
Apply the preference for not using a wudu towel
The text states that the preferred (al-ula) is not to pray on a towel used for wiping after wudu. This is a guideline of adab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المأثور. كل ذكر فات محله لم يأتِ به فلا يكمل التسبيحات بعد رفع رأسه، ولا يأتي بالتسميع بعد رفع رأسه من الركوع . صلى مكشوف الرأس لم يكره. الرباعية المسنونة كالفرض فلا يصلي في القعدة الأولى ولا يستفتح إذا قام إلى الثالثة إلا في حق القراءة فإنها واجبة في جميع ركعاتها، يقرأ في كل ركعة الفاتحة والسورة. الأولى ألأ يصلى على منديل الوضوء الذي يمسح به. كل صلاة أُديت مع ترك. واجب أو فعل مكروه تحريما، فإنها تُعاد وجوبًا في الوقت فإن خرج لا تُعاد. إذا رفع رأسه قبل إمامه فإنه يعود إلى السجود من جمع بأهله لا ينال ثواب الجماعة إلا إذا كان لعذر دخل المسجد في الفجر فوجد الإمام يصليه فإنه يأتي بالسنة بعيدًا عن الصفوف إلا إذا خاف سلام الإمام مسجد المحلة أفضل من الجامع إلا إذا كان إمامه عالما ومسجد المحلة في حق السوقي نهارًا ما كان عند حانوته، وليلاً ما كان عند منزله
Established. Every dhikr whose place passed and he did not perform it, so he does not complete the tasbihat after raising his head, and he does not perform the tasmi' after raising his head from bowing. He prayed with head uncovered: it is not disliked. The four-rak'ah sunnah is like the obligatory, so he does not pray in the first sitting and does not recite the opening supplication when he stands for the third, except regarding recitation, for it is obligatory in all its rak'ahs; he recites al-Fatihah and a surah in every rak'ah. The preferred: he should not pray on the wudu towel with which he wipes. Every prayer performed with leaving an obligatory or doing something prohibitively disliked: it is repeated obligatorily within the time; if the time leaves, it is not repeated. If he raises his head before his imam, he returns to prostration. Whoever gathers his family does not attain the reward of congregation unless there is an excuse. He entered the mosque at Fajr and found the imam praying it: he performs the sunnah away from the rows unless he fears the imam's salutation. The mosque of the locality is better than the congregational mosque unless his imam is knowledgeable. And the locality mosque for the market-goer by day is where his shop is, and by night where his home is.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rasm rulings (established rules) for the mufti. It begins with the rule that if one misses a dhikr in its proper place (e.g., tasmi' after rising from bowing), he does not make it up later; he simply omits it. Praying with uncovered head is not disliked (makruh) according to the Hanafi school. The four-rak'ah sunnah prayers (like sunnah of Zuhr) are treated like obligatory prayer in terms of not sitting for tashahhud after two rak'ahs and not reciting the opening supplication when standing for the third; but recitation of Fatihah and a surah is wajib in every rak'ah. It is better not to pray on a towel used for wiping after wudu. Any prayer performed with the omission of a wajib or the commission of a makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked act) must be repeated within its time; after the time exits, repetition is not required. If a follower raises his head before the imam in prostration, he must return. Gathering one's family for prayer at home does not earn the reward of congregation unless there is a valid excuse. Entering the mosque at Fajr and finding the imam already in the fard prayer: the follower should perform the sunnah away from the rows unless he fears missing the imam's salutation. The local mosque (masjid al-mahallah) is superior to the main congregational mosque (jami') unless the imam of the jami' is more learned. For a market-goer, his 'neighborhood mosque' is defined by location: near his shop by day, near his home by night.

Key Terms
المأثور (al-ma'thūr): Established; used to denote a fixed ruling from the early sources.
التسبيحات (al-tasbīḥāt): The utterances of glorification (Subhan Allah) in bowing and prostration.
التسميع (al-tasmīʿ): Saying 'Sami Allahu liman hamidah' after rising from bowing.
مكشوف الرأس (makshūf al-ra's): Uncovered head; praying without head covering.
منديل الوضوء (mandīl al-wuḍūʾ): The towel used for drying after wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They should say it now.
B) They should perform sajdah al-sahw.
C) They should not say it later.
D) They should repeat the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Missed sunnah dhikr is not compensated after its place; head uncovered is permissible; it is preferred not to pray on a wudu towel.

Rulings on Four-Rak'ah Sunnah and Invalid Prayer
This passage gives two distinct rasm rulings: the first on the form of the four-rak'ah sunnah, the second on repetition of prayer due to violation of wajib or makruh tahrimi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rules for four-rak'ah sunnah prayers (no first sitting, no opening dua, recitation wajib in all rak'ahs) and the rule on repeating a prayer that contains a missed wajib or a makruh tahrimi.

Core Idea
Four-rak'ah sunnah follows fard pattern in sitting and opening dua but recitation is wajib in all rak'ahs; a prayer with a missed wajib must be repeated within time.

This lesson presents two important rulings: the form of the four-rak'ah sunnah prayer (like fard in some aspects) and the general principle that a prayer violated by omission of a wajib or commission of a makruh tahrimi must be repeated within its prescribed time.

Guided Path
1
Understand the rule for four-rak'ah sunnah
The sunnah of Zuhr, Asr, and Isha (if prayed as four) is like the fard: you do not sit after two rak'ahs and do not recite the opening du'a when standing for the third.
But recitation of al-Fatihah and a surah is wajib in every rak'ah.
2
Apply the exception for recitation
Unlike the fard where recitation is only wajib in the first two rak'ahs, in sunnah it is wajib in all four.
3
Apply the rule for invalid prayer
Any prayer performed while missing a wajib action or doing a makruh tahrimi act must be repeated within its time. If the time passes, no repetition is required.
The prayer is still valid but deficient and sinful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المأثور. كل ذكر فات محله لم يأتِ به فلا يكمل التسبيحات بعد رفع رأسه، ولا يأتي بالتسميع بعد رفع رأسه من الركوع . صلى مكشوف الرأس لم يكره. الرباعية المسنونة كالفرض فلا يصلي في القعدة الأولى ولا يستفتح إذا قام إلى الثالثة إلا في حق القراءة فإنها واجبة في جميع ركعاتها، يقرأ في كل ركعة الفاتحة والسورة. الأولى ألأ يصلى على منديل الوضوء الذي يمسح به. كل صلاة أُديت مع ترك. واجب أو فعل مكروه تحريما، فإنها تُعاد وجوبًا في الوقت فإن خرج لا تُعاد. إذا رفع رأسه قبل إمامه فإنه يعود إلى السجود من جمع بأهله لا ينال ثواب الجماعة إلا إذا كان لعذر دخل المسجد في الفجر فوجد الإمام يصليه فإنه يأتي بالسنة بعيدًا عن الصفوف إلا إذا خاف سلام الإمام مسجد المحلة أفضل من الجامع إلا إذا كان إمامه عالما ومسجد المحلة في حق السوقي نهارًا ما كان عند حانوته، وليلاً ما كان عند منزله
Established. Every dhikr whose place passed and he did not perform it, so he does not complete the tasbihat after raising his head, and he does not perform the tasmi' after raising his head from bowing. He prayed with head uncovered: it is not disliked. The four-rak'ah sunnah is like the obligatory, so he does not pray in the first sitting and does not recite the opening supplication when he stands for the third, except regarding recitation, for it is obligatory in all its rak'ahs; he recites al-Fatihah and a surah in every rak'ah. The preferred: he should not pray on the wudu towel with which he wipes. Every prayer performed with leaving an obligatory or doing something prohibitively disliked: it is repeated obligatorily within the time; if the time leaves, it is not repeated. If he raises his head before his imam, he returns to prostration. Whoever gathers his family does not attain the reward of congregation unless there is an excuse. He entered the mosque at Fajr and found the imam praying it: he performs the sunnah away from the rows unless he fears the imam's salutation. The mosque of the locality is better than the congregational mosque unless his imam is knowledgeable. And the locality mosque for the market-goer by day is where his shop is, and by night where his home is.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rasm rulings (established rules) for the mufti. It begins with the rule that if one misses a dhikr in its proper place (e.g., tasmi' after rising from bowing), he does not make it up later; he simply omits it. Praying with uncovered head is not disliked (makruh) according to the Hanafi school. The four-rak'ah sunnah prayers (like sunnah of Zuhr) are treated like obligatory prayer in terms of not sitting for tashahhud after two rak'ahs and not reciting the opening supplication when standing for the third; but recitation of Fatihah and a surah is wajib in every rak'ah. It is better not to pray on a towel used for wiping after wudu. Any prayer performed with the omission of a wajib or the commission of a makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked act) must be repeated within its time; after the time exits, repetition is not required. If a follower raises his head before the imam in prostration, he must return. Gathering one's family for prayer at home does not earn the reward of congregation unless there is a valid excuse. Entering the mosque at Fajr and finding the imam already in the fard prayer: the follower should perform the sunnah away from the rows unless he fears missing the imam's salutation. The local mosque (masjid al-mahallah) is superior to the main congregational mosque (jami') unless the imam of the jami' is more learned. For a market-goer, his 'neighborhood mosque' is defined by location: near his shop by day, near his home by night.

Key Terms
الرباعية المسنونة (al-rubāʿiyya al-masnūna): The four-rak'ah sunnah prayer (e.g., sunnah of Zuhr, Asr, Isha).
القعدة الأولى (al-qaʿda al-ūlā): The first sitting after two rak'ahs.
الاستفتاح (al-istiftāḥ): The opening supplication (Subhanakallahumma...) recited at the start of the prayer.
مكروه تحريما (makrūh taḥrīman): Prohibitively disliked; an act that is haram to do but does not invalidate the prayer by itself, though it requires repetition.
تعاد وجوبًا (tuʿādu wujūban): It is repeated as an obligation (wajib).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone omits a wajib in a prayer, what is the ruling according to this passage?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated at any time.
B) The prayer is valid and no action needed.
C) The prayer must be repeated within its time.
D) The prayer must be repeated with sajdah al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
Four-rak'ah sunnah: no first sitting, no opening dua, but recitation wajib in all rak'ahs; prayer with wajib omission or makruh tahrimi repeated within time.

Rulings on Following the Imam and Mosque Preference
This passage gives four distinct rasm rulings: (1) follower returning to prostration, (2) family prayer reward, (3) sunnah in mosque during fajr, (4) mosque preference and definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on: returning to prostration if the follower raises his head early, conditions for earning congregational reward, performing sunnah when entering mosque during fajr, and the preference between local and jami' mosque.

Core Idea
Follower must imitate imam strictly; gathering family at home does not earn congregational reward without excuse; local mosque is preferred unless jami' imam is more learned; local mosque definition varies by time of day.

This lesson presents several practical rulings related to congregational prayer and mosque choice. A mufti should know these to guide the community on issues like arriving late, family prayer, and mosque attendance.

Guided Path
1
Rule on follower raising head before imam
If a follower raises his head from prostration before the imam, he must return to prostration and follow the imam.
This ensures proper adherence to the imam.
2
Rule on gathering family at home
Gathering one's family for prayer at home does not give the full reward of congregation unless there is a valid excuse (e.g., illness, weather).
Congregation in the mosque is preferred.
3
Rule on sunnah when entering mosque during fajr
If one enters the mosque at Fajr and finds the imam already in the fard prayer, he should perform the sunnah away from the rows unless he fears missing the imam's salutation; in that case, he joins the congregation.
This balances between sunnah and congregation.
4
Rule on mosque preference
The local mosque (masjid al-mahallah) is generally better to pray in than the main congregational mosque (jami'), unless the imam of the jami' is more knowledgeable.
This encourages community cohesion.
5
Definition of local mosque for market-goer
For a market-goer, his 'local mosque' by day is the one near his shop, and by night the one near his home.
The ruling takes into account a person's daily routine.

المأثور. كل ذكر فات محله لم يأتِ به فلا يكمل التسبيحات بعد رفع رأسه، ولا يأتي بالتسميع بعد رفع رأسه من الركوع . صلى مكشوف الرأس لم يكره. الرباعية المسنونة كالفرض فلا يصلي في القعدة الأولى ولا يستفتح إذا قام إلى الثالثة إلا في حق القراءة فإنها واجبة في جميع ركعاتها، يقرأ في كل ركعة الفاتحة والسورة. الأولى ألأ يصلى على منديل الوضوء الذي يمسح به. كل صلاة أُديت مع ترك. واجب أو فعل مكروه تحريما، فإنها تُعاد وجوبًا في الوقت فإن خرج لا تُعاد. إذا رفع رأسه قبل إمامه فإنه يعود إلى السجود من جمع بأهله لا ينال ثواب الجماعة إلا إذا كان لعذر دخل المسجد في الفجر فوجد الإمام يصليه فإنه يأتي بالسنة بعيدًا عن الصفوف إلا إذا خاف سلام الإمام مسجد المحلة أفضل من الجامع إلا إذا كان إمامه عالما ومسجد المحلة في حق السوقي نهارًا ما كان عند حانوته، وليلاً ما كان عند منزله
Established. Every dhikr whose place passed and he did not perform it, so he does not complete the tasbihat after raising his head, and he does not perform the tasmi' after raising his head from bowing. He prayed with head uncovered: it is not disliked. The four-rak'ah sunnah is like the obligatory, so he does not pray in the first sitting and does not recite the opening supplication when he stands for the third, except regarding recitation, for it is obligatory in all its rak'ahs; he recites al-Fatihah and a surah in every rak'ah. The preferred: he should not pray on the wudu towel with which he wipes. Every prayer performed with leaving an obligatory or doing something prohibitively disliked: it is repeated obligatorily within the time; if the time leaves, it is not repeated. If he raises his head before his imam, he returns to prostration. Whoever gathers his family does not attain the reward of congregation unless there is an excuse. He entered the mosque at Fajr and found the imam praying it: he performs the sunnah away from the rows unless he fears the imam's salutation. The mosque of the locality is better than the congregational mosque unless his imam is knowledgeable. And the locality mosque for the market-goer by day is where his shop is, and by night where his home is.

الجامع (al-jāmiʿ): The main congregational mosque where Friday prayer is held.

Rulings on Iqtida' and Recitation Basics
Set of rasm rulings on prayer and iqtida

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on arranging surahs, shortening recitation in Fajr sunnah, and the conditions for valid iqtida' for men and women.

Core Idea
A man can follow another without the imam's intention; a woman needs it except in Jumu'ah and 'Eid.

This lesson covers a set of foundational rasm rulings from Hanafi fiqh. We begin with the arrangement of surahs in prayer, etiquette of recitation, and then delve into the essential conditions for following an imam (iqtida'). These rulings are part of the mufti's toolkit for answering common prayer questions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on arranging surahs
The passage states it is disliked (makruh) not to arrange surahs in order of revelation, except in supererogatory prayers. Note when this ruling applies.
2
Determine the status of speech between sunnah and fard
Speech between the sunnah and fard does not invalidate the prayer but decreases reward. This shows the importance of maintaining sequence.
3
Analyze the conditions for valid iqtida' for men
A man can validly follow another man even if the imam did not intend to lead. This is a unique Hanafi rule.
4
Analyze the conditions for valid iqtida' for women
A woman's following is only valid if the imam intended her imamah, except in Jumu'ah and 'Eid where his intention suffices even in their absence.
This exception is important in practice.
5
Evaluate the effect of thoughts and distractions
Reflecting on non-prayer matters does not invalidate the prayer, and loss of khushu' due to worldly concerns does not reduce reward if not from negligence.
Distinguish between invalidation and loss of perfection.

يُكرَه ألا يُرَتِّب بين السور إلا في النافلة تقليل القراءة في سنة الفجر أفضل من تطويلها. نذره النافلة أفضل وقيل لا التكلّم بين السُّنَّة والفرض لا تُسقطها، ولكن ينقص الثواب. يُكره أن يخصص لصلاته مكانا في المسجد وإن فعله فسبقه غيره لا يزعجه. يكون شارعا بالتكبير إلا إذا أراد به التعجب دون التعظيم. إذا تفكر المصلّي في غير صلاته كتجارته ودرسه لم تبطل . وإن شغله همومه عن خشوعه لم ينقص أجره إن لم يكن عن تقصير، ولا تستحب إعادتها لترك الخشوع. لا ينبغي للمؤذن والإمام انتظار أحد إلا أن يكون شريرًا. يصح اقتداء الرجل بالمصلي وإن لم ينو إمامته، ولا يصح اقتداء المرأة إلا إذا نوى إمامتها إلا في الجمعة والعيدين وتصح نية إمامتهنَّ في غيبتهنَّ . خرج الخطيب بعد شروعه متنفلاً، قطع على رأس الركعتين إلا إذا كان في سُنّة الجمعة فإنه يتمها على الصحيح لم يجد إلا ثوب حرير يصلي فيه بلا خيار، بخلاف الثوب النجس حيث يتخير فإن لم يجد إلا هما صلى في الحرير. الاقتداء فناء المسجد كالمسجد فيصح الاقتداء وإن لم تتصل الصفوف المانع من طريق تمرّ فيه العجلة أو نهر تجري فيه السفن أو خلاء في الصحراء يسع صفين . والخلاء في المسجد لا يمنع وإن وسع صفوفًا، لأن له حكم بقعة واحدة. واختلفوا في الحائل بينهما، والأصح الصحة إذا كان لا يشتبه عليه حال إمامه. المسافر إذا لم يقعد على رأس الركعتين فإنها تبطل إذا نوى الإقامة قبل أن يقيد الثالثة بسجدة. الأسير إذا خلص يقضي صلاة المقيمين إلا إذ رحل العدوّ به إلى مكان أراد الإقامة في خمسة عشر يوما فيقضيها صلاة المسافرين ولمن به شقيقة برأسه الإيماء. لو كان المريض بحال لو خرج إلى الجماعة لا يقدر على القيام ولو صلّى في بيته قدر عليه، الأصح أنه يخرج ويصلّي قاعدًا لأن الفرض مقدر بحاله على الاقتداء وعلى اعتباره سقط القيام واختلفوا في مريض إن قام لا يقدر على مراعاة سُنَّة القراءة، وإن قعد قدر الأصح أنه يقعد ويراعيها قدر المريض على بعض القيام قام بقدره. إذا كرر آية سجدة واحدة في مجلس واحد فالأفضل الاكتفاء بسجدة واحدة، وإذا كرّر اسم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فالأفضل تكرار الصلاة عليه وإن كفاه واحدة فيهما، ولا يرفع يديه في سجود التلاوة ولا فدية لسجود التلاوة ولا تجب نيَّة التعيين لها، والسنة القيام لها. إذا قرأ الإمام آية سجدة فالأفضل الركوع لها إن كان في صلاة المخافتة وإلا القرآنية بقصد الثناء؛ فلو قرأ الجُنُب الفاتحة بقصد الثناء لم يحرم ولو قصد بها الثناء في الجنازة لم يُكره إلا إذا قرأ المصلي قاصدًا الثناء فإنها تجزيه. لا رياء في الفرائض في حق سقوطها. إذا أراد فعل طاعة وخاف الرياء لا يتركها قراءة الفاتحة لأجل الممات عقب المكتوبة بدعة.

قال الشيخ محمد علي الطرابلسي في تعليقاته ص ٨٥ : (هذا) ضعيف، والصحيح الاقتداء به في الوتر إن لم يسلم على رأس الركعتين، وعدم الصحة إن سلم وقيل يصح الاقتداء، وإن سلم، ولا يضر كون الوتر سُنَّة عند الشافعي، وعند الحنفي واجبًا لأن اعتقاد الوجوب ليس بواجب على الحنفي، ومنه يعلم خطأ من اعتقد فساد اقتداء الحنفي بالشافعي في صلاة العيدين محتجا بأنه اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل لما ذكر).

القراءة في الحمام جهرًا مكروه وسرًا لا وهو المختار ولا يُكره للمحدث من كتب الفقه والحديث على الأصح وضع المقلمة على الكتاب مكروه إلا لأجل الكتابة، وضع المصحف تحت رأسه مكروه إلا للحفظ لا ينبغي تأقيت الدعاء إلا في الصلاة. يُكره الاقتداء في صلاة الرغائب وصلاة البراءة وليلة القدر، إلا إذا قال نذرت كذا ركعة بهذا الإمام بالجماعة كذا في البزازية. تعدّد السهو لا يُوجب تعدّد السجود إلا في المسبوق. يُكرَه الأذان قاعدًا إلا لنفسه الإسفار بالفجر أفضل إلا بمزدلفة للحاج. تأخير المغرب مكروه إلا في السفر أو على مائدة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم .
It is disliked not to arrange between surahs except in supererogatory prayer. Shortening recitation in the sunnah of Fajr is better than lengthening it. His nadhr supererogatory prayer is better – and it is said not. Speech between the sunnah and fard does not invalidate it, but decreases reward. It is disliked to designate a specific place in the mosque for his prayer; if he does so and someone else precedes him, he should not disturb him. He becomes started with the takbir unless he intends amazement rather than magnification. If the praying person reflects on other than his prayer, like his trade or study, it does not invalidate. If concerns distract him from his khushu‘, his reward is not diminished if it is not due to negligence; nor is it recommended to repeat it for leaving khushu‘. It is not befitting for the mu’adhdhin and imam to wait for anyone unless he is malicious. A man’s following one who is praying is valid even if he did not intend him to be imam; a woman’s following is not valid unless he intended her imamah except in Jumu‘ah and the two ‘Eids; and his intention of imamah for them is valid in their absence. The khatib after his commencement in supererogatory prayer cuts off at the end of two rak‘ahs unless in the sunnah of Jumu‘ah, then he completes it according to the sound view. He finds only a silk garment: he prays in it with no choice, unlike a najis garment where he has a choice; if he finds only the two, he prays in silk. Following in the courtyard of the mosque is like in the mosque, so following is valid even if rows are not connected. The preventer is a road where a carriage passes, or a river where ships sail, or an empty space in the desert that accommodates two rows. But emptiness in the mosque is not a preventer even if it accommodates rows, because it has the ruling of one place. They disagreed about a barrier between them; the sound view is validity if his imam’s situation is not ambiguous to him. The traveler: if he did not sit at the end of two rak‘ahs, it becomes invalid if he intended residence before tying the third with a prostration. The captive: when he is freed, he prays the prayers of residents unless the enemy traveled with him to a place where he intended residence for fifteen days, then he prays them as traveler’s prayers. For one with migraine, he signals with his head. If the patient is such that if he goes out to congregation he cannot stand, but if he prays at home he can stand, the sound view is that he goes out and prays sitting, because the fard is estimated according to his situation; and upon that consideration, standing falls. They disagreed about a patient who, if he stands, cannot observe the sunnah of recitation, but if he sits he can – the sound view is that he sits and observes it. A patient who can partially stand stands according to his ability. If he repeats one prostration verse in one sitting, the best is to suffice with one prostration. If he repeats the Prophet’s name ﷺ, the best is to repeat the blessing upon him, though one suffices in both. He does not raise his hands in sujud al-tilawah, nor is there any fidyah for it, nor is specifying the intention obligatory for it; and the sunnah is to stand for it. If the imam recites a prostration verse, the best is to bow for it if in a silent prayer, otherwise he prostrates for it. It is disliked to intentionally leave the surah in the last two of supererogatory prayer; if he forgets, he must perform sahw. If he adds it in another fard inadvertently, he does not prostrate, and upon it is the fatwa: it is not permissible to follow the Shafi‘i in witr. And if it is not that the Qur’an is cut off, it becomes non-Qur’anic by the intention of praise. So if a junub recites al-Fatihah with the intention of praise, it is not haram. If he intends praise with it in janazah, it is not disliked. But if the praying person recites intending praise, it suffices him. There is no riya’ in obligatory acts with respect to their validity. If he intends to do an act of obedience and fears riya’, he should not abandon it. Reciting al-Fatihah for the deceased after the prescribed prayer is an innovation. (1) Al-Shaykh Muhammad ‘Ali al-Tarabulsi said in his commentaries p. 85: “This is weak; the correct is that it is permissible to follow him in witr if he did not give salams at end of two rak‘ahs; and if he gave salams, it is not valid – and it is said it is valid even if he gave salams. And it does not harm that witr is sunnah according to Shafi‘i and wajib according to Hanafi, because believing it wajib is not obligatory for the Hanafi. From this one knows the error of whoever believes the invalidity of a Hanafi following a Shafi‘i in the prayer of the two ‘Eids, arguing that it is the following of one performing fard by one performing nafl due to what was mentioned.” (new line) Recitation in the bathroom aloud is disliked; silently, it is not – and that is the chosen view. It is not disliked for the one with hadath to touch books of fiqh and hadith according to the sound view. Placing a pen case on the book is disliked except for the sake of writing. Placing the mushaf under the head is disliked except for memorization. It is not proper to specify a fixed time for du‘a’ except in prayer. It is disliked to follow in the prayer of Ragha’ib, and the prayer of Bara’ah, and Laylat al-Qadr, unless he says: “I vowed such-and-such rak‘ahs with this imam in congregation” as in al-Bazzaziyyah. Multiplicity of forgetfulness does not necessitate multiplicity of prostrations except for the masbuq. It is disliked to give adhan while sitting unless for oneself. Dawn light (isfar) is better except at Muzdalifah for the pilgrim. Delaying Maghrib is disliked except while traveling or upon a spread. And Allah Almighty knows best.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This long passage is a detailed collection of rasm rulings (fixed rules) for the mufti, covering many aspects of prayer and related matters. It begins by stating that it is disliked (makruh) not to arrange surahs in order of revelation in supererogatory prayers, except in nafl. Shortening recitation in Fajr sunnah is better than lengthening it. Vowed supererogatory prayers are superior – with disagreement. Speaking between sunnah and fard does not invalidate either, but reduces reward. Designating a fixed spot in the mosque for prayer is disliked; if someone else takes it, do not oust them. One becomes in prayer with the takbir unless the intention was pure amazement. Inner thoughts foreign to prayer (like trade or study) do not invalidate the prayer. Loss of khushu‘ due to worldly concerns does not reduce reward if not from negligence, and repeating such a prayer is not recommended. The mu’adhdhin and imam should not wait for latecomers except a troublesome person. A man can validly follow another man in prayer even if the latter did not intend to be imam; a woman cannot follow a man unless he intended her imamah – except in Jumu‘ah and ‘Eid prayers, where his intention of their imamah is valid even if they are absent. A khatib who starts a supererogatory prayer must cut it off after two rak’ahs, unless it is the sunnah of Jumu’ah (then he completes it). If only a silk garment is available, one must pray in it without choice (to cover); but if both a silk and a najis garment are available, one chooses between them. Following in the courtyard of the mosque is like following inside; gaps in rows do not invalidate as long as there is no major barrier like a wide road or river. Emptiness of rows within the mosque is not a barrier. A barrier (like a wall) between imam and follower: the soundest opinion is validity if the follower is not confused about the imam’s actions. A traveler who does not sit after two rak’ahs: if he intended residence before tying the third rak’ah, his prayer becomes invalid. A captive upon release prays as a resident unless he resided fifteen days in enemy territory. A migraine sufferer may signal. A patient who cannot stand in congregation but can stand at home should go to the mosque and pray sitting. A patient who can only observe correct recitation while sitting should sit. When repeating the same prostration verse in one sitting, one sufficing prostration is best; repeating the Prophet’s name likewise best with repeated blessings, though one suffices. Hands are not raised in sujud al-tilawah; no fidyah; specific intention for it is not obligatory; standing is sunnah. An imam in a silent prayer should bow for the prostration verse; otherwise, he prostrates. Deliberately omitting a surah in the last two rak’ahs of a nafl is disliked; if forgotten, sahw prostrations are required. Adding a surah in a fard after the second rak’ah inadvertently does not require sahw. The fatwa is that a Hanafi may not follow a Shafi‘i in witr (with a detailed footnote from Tarabulsi clarifying exceptions). A junub reciting Fatihah with the intention of praise is not haram. Intending praise in janazah is not disliked. Riya‘ does not affect validity of obligatory acts. If one fears riya’ in an act of obedience, do not abandon it. Reciting Fatihah for the deceased after fard is innovation. Then follow miscellaneous rulings: reciting aloud in bathroom disliked; silent recitation not disliked. Touching books of fiqh/hadith is not disliked for one in hadath. Placing a pen case on a book is disliked except for writing. Placing mushaf under head is disliked except for memorization. Fixing a time for du‘a‘ outside prayer is not proper. Following in innovated prayers (Ragha’ib, Bara’ah, Laylat al-Qadr) is disliked unless vowed. Multiple forgetfulness does not multiply sajw except for masbuq. Adhan while sitting disliked unless for oneself. Making Fajr dawn prayer early (isfar) is better except at Muzdalifah. Delaying Maghrib is disliked except when traveling or eating. And Allah knows best.

Key Terms
مكروه تحريما (makrūh taḥrīman): An action that is prohibitively disliked, close to haram; repeating the prayer for it is obligatory within the time.
اقتداء (iqtiḍā’): Following an imam in congregational prayer; rules about who can follow whom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a woman's following of an imam valid without his specific intention?
A) In all prayers
B) In Jumu'ah and 'Eid prayers
C) Only in Fajr prayer
D) Never valid

Key Takeaway
A man can follow any praying person without their intention; a woman needs the imam's intention except for Jumu'ah and 'Eid.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate

Sujud al-Tilawah, Barriers, and Special Cases in Prayer
Rasm rulings on sujud al-tilawah, barriers, and prayer modifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on sujud al-tilawah, barriers affecting iqtida, and prayer modifications for traveler, captive, and patient.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah does not require lifting hands or specific intention; a barrier between imam and follower is no issue unless it causes confusion.

The passage continues with a series of practical rulings. Understanding these helps a mufti address common questions about prostration of recitation, when a barrier between rows is acceptable, and how travelers, captives, and patients should pray. Each rule has specific conditions.

Guided Path
1
Examine rulings on sujud al-tilawah
The passage covers repetition of sujud verse, no hand raising, no fidyah, no specific intention needed, and sunnah to stand. Identify each ruling.
2
Define the barriers that prevent iqtida
A road, river, or desert space with room for two rows prevents validity; but emptiness within a mosque does not. A barrier like a wall: valid if the follower is not confused about the imam's actions.
3
Apply rulings for traveler and captive
Traveler who does not sit after two rak'ahs: prayer invalid if he intended residence before the third rak'ah sajdah. Captive upon release prays as resident unless he resided 15 days in enemy territory.
4
Analyze rulings for the patient
A patient who can stand at home but not in congregation should go out and pray sitting; if standing harms recitation quality, he sits. Partial ability to stand requires partial standing.
5
Interpret the imam's handling of prostration verse
If imam recites sajdah verse, best is to bow if in silent prayer, otherwise prostrate.

Source Text

يُكرَه ألا يُرَتِّب بين السور إلا في النافلة تقليل القراءة في سنة الفجر أفضل من تطويلها. نذره النافلة أفضل وقيل لا التكلّم بين السُّنَّة والفرض لا تُسقطها، ولكن ينقص الثواب. يُكره أن يخصص لصلاته مكانا في المسجد وإن فعله فسبقه غيره لا يزعجه. يكون شارعا بالتكبير إلا إذا أراد به التعجب دون التعظيم. إذا تفكر المصلّي في غير صلاته كتجارته ودرسه لم تبطل . وإن شغله همومه عن خشوعه لم ينقص أجره إن لم يكن عن تقصير، ولا تستحب إعادتها لترك الخشوع. لا ينبغي للمؤذن والإمام انتظار أحد إلا أن يكون شريرًا. يصح اقتداء الرجل بالمصلي وإن لم ينو إمامته، ولا يصح اقتداء المرأة إلا إذا نوى إمامتها إلا في الجمعة والعيدين وتصح نية إمامتهنَّ في غيبتهنَّ . خرج الخطيب بعد شروعه متنفلاً، قطع على رأس الركعتين إلا إذا كان في سُنّة الجمعة فإنه يتمها على الصحيح لم يجد إلا ثوب حرير يصلي فيه بلا خيار، بخلاف الثوب النجس حيث يتخير فإن لم يجد إلا هما صلى في الحرير. الاقتداء فناء المسجد كالمسجد فيصح الاقتداء وإن لم تتصل الصفوف المانع من طريق تمرّ فيه العجلة أو نهر تجري فيه السفن أو خلاء في الصحراء يسع صفين . والخلاء في المسجد لا يمنع وإن وسع صفوفًا، لأن له حكم بقعة واحدة. واختلفوا في الحائل بينهما، والأصح الصحة إذا كان لا يشتبه عليه حال إمامه. المسافر إذا لم يقعد على رأس الركعتين فإنها تبطل إذا نوى الإقامة قبل أن يقيد الثالثة بسجدة. الأسير إذا خلص يقضي صلاة المقيمين إلا إذ رحل العدوّ به إلى مكان أراد الإقامة في خمسة عشر يوما فيقضيها صلاة المسافرين ولمن به شقيقة برأسه الإيماء. لو كان المريض بحال لو خرج إلى الجماعة لا يقدر على القيام ولو صلّى في بيته قدر عليه، الأصح أنه يخرج ويصلّي قاعدًا لأن الفرض مقدر بحاله على الاقتداء وعلى اعتباره سقط القيام واختلفوا في مريض إن قام لا يقدر على مراعاة سُنَّة القراءة، وإن قعد قدر الأصح أنه يقعد ويراعيها قدر المريض على بعض القيام قام بقدره. إذا كرر آية سجدة واحدة في مجلس واحد فالأفضل الاكتفاء بسجدة واحدة، وإذا كرّر اسم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فالأفضل تكرار الصلاة عليه وإن كفاه واحدة فيهما، ولا يرفع يديه في سجود التلاوة ولا فدية لسجود التلاوة ولا تجب نيَّة التعيين لها، والسنة القيام لها. إذا قرأ الإمام آية سجدة فالأفضل الركوع لها إن كان في صلاة المخافتة وإلا سجد لها. يُكرَه ترك السورة في الأخريين من التطوّع عمدا، وإن سها فعليه السهو، ولو ضمها في أخرى الفرض ساهيًا لا يسجد وعليه الفتوى لا يجوز الاقتداء بالشافعي في الوتر ) وإن كان لا يقطعه القرآن يخرج عن القرآنية بقصد الثناء؛ فلو قرأ الجُنُب الفاتحة بقصد الثناء لم يحرم ولو قصد بها الثناء في الجنازة لم يُكره إلا إذا قرأ المصلي قاصدًا الثناء فإنها تجزيه. لا رياء في الفرائض في حق سقوطها. إذا أراد فعل طاعة وخاف الرياء لا يتركها قراءة الفاتحة لأجل الممات عقب المكتوبة بدعة.
(1)
قال الشيخ محمد علي الطرابلسي في تعليقاته ص ٨٥ : (هذا) ضعيف، والصحيح الاقتداء به في الوتر إن لم يسلم على رأس الركعتين، وعدم الصحة إن سلم وقيل يصح الاقتداء، وإن سلم، ولا يضر كون الوتر سُنَّة عند الشافعي، وعند الحنفي واجبًا لأن اعتقاد الوجوب ليس بواجب على الحنفي، ومنه يعلم خطأ من اعتقد فساد اقتداء الحنفي بالشافعي في صلاة العيدين محتجا بأنه اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل لما ذكر).
·
القراءة في الحمام جهرًا مكروه وسرًا لا وهو المختار ولا يُكره للمحدث من كتب الفقه والحديث على الأصح وضع المقلمة على الكتاب مكروه إلا لأجل الكتابة، وضع المصحف تحت رأسه مكروه إلا للحفظ لا ينبغي تأقيت الدعاء إلا في الصلاة. يُكره الاقتداء في صلاة الرغائب وصلاة البراءة وليلة القدر، إلا إذا قال نذرت كذا ركعة بهذا الإمام بالجماعة كذا في البزازية. تعدّد السهو لا يُوجب تعدّد السجود إلا في المسبوق. يُكرَه الأذان قاعدًا إلا لنفسه الإسفار بالفجر أفضل إلا بمزدلفة للحاج. تأخير المغرب مكروه إلا في السفر أو على مائدة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم .
It is disliked not to arrange between surahs except in supererogatory prayer. Shortening recitation in the sunnah of Fajr is better than lengthening it. His nadhr supererogatory prayer is better – and it is said not. Speech between the sunnah and fard does not invalidate it, but decreases reward. It is disliked to designate a specific place in the mosque for his prayer; if he does so and someone else precedes him, he should not disturb him. He becomes started with the takbir unless he intends amazement rather than magnification. If the praying person reflects on other than his prayer, like his trade or study, it does not invalidate. If concerns distract him from his khushu‘, his reward is not diminished if it is not due to negligence; nor is it recommended to repeat it for leaving khushu‘. It is not befitting for the mu’adhdhin and imam to wait for anyone unless he is malicious. A man’s following one who is praying is valid even if he did not intend him to be imam; a woman’s following is not valid unless he intended her imamah except in Jumu‘ah and the two ‘Eids; and his intention of imamah for them is valid in their absence. The khatib after his commencement in supererogatory prayer cuts off at the end of two rak‘ahs unless in the sunnah of Jumu‘ah, then he completes it according to the sound view. He finds only a silk garment: he prays in it with no choice, unlike a najis garment where he has a choice; if he finds only the two, he prays in silk. Following in the courtyard of the mosque is like in the mosque, so following is valid even if rows are not connected. The preventer is a road where a carriage passes, or a river where ships sail, or an empty space in the desert that accommodates two rows. But emptiness in the mosque is not a preventer even if it accommodates rows, because it has the ruling of one place. They disagreed about a barrier between them; the sound view is validity if his imam’s situation is not ambiguous to him. The traveler: if he did not sit at the end of two rak‘ahs, it becomes invalid if he intended residence before tying the third with a prostration. The captive: when he is freed, he prays the prayers of residents unless the enemy traveled with him to a place where he intended residence for fifteen days, then he prays them as traveler’s prayers. For one with migraine, he signals with his head. If the patient is such that if he goes out to congregation he cannot stand, but if he prays at home he can stand, the sound view is that he goes out and prays sitting, because the fard is estimated according to his situation; and upon that consideration, standing falls. They disagreed about a patient who, if he stands, cannot observe the sunnah of recitation, but if he sits he can – the sound view is that he sits and observes it. A patient who can partially stand stands according to his ability. If he repeats one prostration verse in one sitting, the best is to suffice with one prostration. If he repeats the Prophet’s name ﷺ, the best is to repeat the blessing upon him, though one suffices in both. He does not raise his hands in sujud al-tilawah, nor is there any fidyah for it, nor is specifying the intention obligatory for it; and the sunnah is to stand for it. If the imam recites a prostration verse, the best is to bow for it if in a silent prayer, otherwise he prostrates for it. It is disliked to intentionally leave the surah in the last two of supererogatory prayer; if he forgets, he must perform sahw. If he adds it in another fard inadvertently, he does not prostrate, and upon it is the fatwa: it is not permissible to follow the Shafi‘i in witr. And if it is not that the Qur’an is cut off, it becomes non-Qur’anic by the intention of praise. So if a junub recites al-Fatihah with the intention of praise, it is not haram. If he intends praise with it in janazah, it is not disliked. But if the praying person recites intending praise, it suffices him. There is no riya’ in obligatory acts with respect to their validity. If he intends to do an act of obedience and fears riya’, he should not abandon it. Reciting al-Fatihah for the deceased after the prescribed prayer is an innovation. (1) Al-Shaykh Muhammad ‘Ali al-Tarabulsi said in his commentaries p. 85: “This is weak; the correct is that it is permissible to follow him in witr if he did not give salams at end of two rak‘ahs; and if he gave salams, it is not valid – and it is said it is valid even if he gave salams. And it does not harm that witr is sunnah according to Shafi‘i and wajib according to Hanafi, because believing it wajib is not obligatory for the Hanafi. From this one knows the error of whoever believes the invalidity of a Hanafi following a Shafi‘i in the prayer of the two ‘Eids, arguing that it is the following of one performing fard by one performing nafl due to what was mentioned.” (new line) Recitation in the bathroom aloud is disliked; silently, it is not – and that is the chosen view. It is not disliked for the one with hadath to touch books of fiqh and hadith according to the sound view. Placing a pen case on the book is disliked except for the sake of writing. Placing the mushaf under the head is disliked except for memorization. It is not proper to specify a fixed time for du‘a’ except in prayer. It is disliked to follow in the prayer of Ragha’ib, and the prayer of Bara’ah, and Laylat al-Qadr, unless he says: “I vowed such-and-such rak‘ahs with this imam in congregation” as in al-Bazzaziyyah. Multiplicity of forgetfulness does not necessitate multiplicity of prostrations except for the masbuq. It is disliked to give adhan while sitting unless for oneself. Dawn light (isfar) is better except at Muzdalifah for the pilgrim. Delaying Maghrib is disliked except while traveling or upon a spread. And Allah Almighty knows best.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This long passage is a detailed collection of rasm rulings (fixed rules) for the mufti, covering many aspects of prayer and related matters. It begins by stating that it is disliked (makruh) not to arrange surahs in order of revelation in supererogatory prayers, except in nafl. Shortening recitation in Fajr sunnah is better than lengthening it. Vowed supererogatory prayers are superior – with disagreement. Speaking between sunnah and fard does not invalidate either, but reduces reward. Designating a fixed spot in the mosque for prayer is disliked; if someone else takes it, do not oust them. One becomes in prayer with the takbir unless the intention was pure amazement. Inner thoughts foreign to prayer (like trade or study) do not invalidate the prayer. Loss of khushu‘ due to worldly concerns does not reduce reward if not from negligence, and repeating such a prayer is not recommended. The mu’adhdhin and imam should not wait for latecomers except a troublesome person. A man can validly follow another man in prayer even if the latter did not intend to be imam; a woman cannot follow a man unless he intended her imamah – except in Jumu‘ah and ‘Eid prayers, where his intention of their imamah is valid even if they are absent. A khatib who starts a supererogatory prayer must cut it off after two rak’ahs, unless it is the sunnah of Jumu’ah (then he completes it). If only a silk garment is available, one must pray in it without choice (to cover); but if both a silk and a najis garment are available, one chooses between them. Following in the courtyard of the mosque is like following inside; gaps in rows do not invalidate as long as there is no major barrier like a wide road or river. Emptiness of rows within the mosque is not a barrier. A barrier (like a wall) between imam and follower: the soundest opinion is validity if the follower is not confused about the imam’s actions. A traveler who does not sit after two rak’ahs: if he intended residence before tying the third rak’ah, his prayer becomes invalid. A captive upon release prays as a resident unless he resided fifteen days in enemy territory. A migraine sufferer may signal. A patient who cannot stand in congregation but can stand at home should go to the mosque and pray sitting. A patient who can only observe correct recitation while sitting should sit. When repeating the same prostration verse in one sitting, one sufficing prostration is best; repeating the Prophet’s name likewise best with repeated blessings, though one suffices. Hands are not raised in sujud al-tilawah; no fidyah; specific intention for it is not obligatory; standing is sunnah. An imam in a silent prayer should bow for the prostration verse; otherwise, he prostrates. Deliberately omitting a surah in the last two rak’ahs of a nafl is disliked; if forgotten, sahw prostrations are required. Adding a surah in a fard after the second rak’ah inadvertently does not require sahw. The fatwa is that a Hanafi may not follow a Shafi‘i in witr (with a detailed footnote from Tarabulsi clarifying exceptions). A junub reciting Fatihah with the intention of praise is not haram. Intending praise in janazah is not disliked. Riya‘ does not affect validity of obligatory acts. If one fears riya’ in an act of obedience, do not abandon it. Reciting Fatihah for the deceased after fard is innovation. Then follow miscellaneous rulings: reciting aloud in bathroom disliked; silent recitation not disliked. Touching books of fiqh/hadith is not disliked for one in hadath. Placing a pen case on a book is disliked except for writing. Placing mushaf under head is disliked except for memorization. Fixing a time for du‘a‘ outside prayer is not proper. Following in innovated prayers (Ragha’ib, Bara’ah, Laylat al-Qadr) is disliked unless vowed. Multiple forgetfulness does not multiply sajw except for masbuq. Adhan while sitting disliked unless for oneself. Making Fajr dawn prayer early (isfar) is better except at Muzdalifah. Delaying Maghrib is disliked except when traveling or eating. And Allah knows best.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujūd al-tilāwah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration in the Quran.
مخافتة (mukhāfatah): Silent prayers (zuhr, 'asr) where recitation is not aloud.
حائل (ḥā’il): A physical barrier (e.g., wall) between imam and follower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on raising hands during sujud al-tilawah according to the passage?
A) It is recommended
B) It is obligatory
C) It is not done (does not raise hands)
D) It is permissible but disliked

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-tilawah is brief: no hand raising, no fidyah, no intention; a barrier in iqtida is only problematic if it blocks knowledge of imam's actions.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
advanced
10 min
The Witr Dispute and Miscellaneous Prayer Rulings
Rasm rulings on witr dispute, forgetfulness, adhan, timing, and novation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on following a Shafi'i in witr, apply the fatwa on multiple forgetfulness, and state the rulings on adhan, timing, and novation.

Core Idea
A Hanafi cannot follow a Shafi'i in witr per the fatwa, but Tarabulsi allows it if the Shafi'i does not give salams after two rak'ahs.

This final segment of the passage addresses the controversial issue of a Hanafi following a Shafi'i in witr prayer, along with a host of miscellaneous rulings. Understanding the dispute and the fatwa hierarchy is essential for muftis dealing with inter-madhhab following. The passage also covers forgetfulness, adhan, timing, and other practical matters.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the witr dispute
The text states the fatwa is that a Hanafi may not follow a Shafi'i in witr. Tarabulsi's footnote gives the correct view being validity if the Shafi'i does not give salams after two rak'ahs. Understand the proof and counter-proof.
2
Distinguish the two opinions
Identify the two positions: (1) prohibition (fatwa), (2) validity with condition (Tarabulsi). Know which is mufta bihi.
3
Apply rulings on multiple forgetfulness
Multiple forgetfulness does not require multiple sujud except for the one who joined late (masbuq).
4
Identify adhan and timing rulings
Adhan while sitting is disliked unless for oneself. Isfar (dawn light) is better except at Muzdalifah. Delaying Maghrib is disliked except when traveling or eating.
5
Evaluate rulings on innovation and novation
Following in innovated prayers (Ragha'ib, Bara'ah, Laylat al-Qadr) is disliked unless vowed. Reciting Fatihah for the deceased after fard is innovation.

والعيدين وتصح نية إمامتهنَّ في غيبتهنَّ . خرج الخطيب بعد شروعه متنفلاً، قطع على رأس الركعتين إلا إذا كان في سُنّة الجمعة فإنه يتمها على الصحيح لم يجد إلا ثوب حرير يصلي فيه بلا خيار، بخلاف الثوب النجس حيث يتخير فإن لم يجد إلا هما صلى في الحرير. الاقتداء فناء المسجد كالمسجد فيصح الاقتداء وإن لم تتصل الصفوف المانع من طريق تمرّ فيه العجلة أو نهر تجري فيه السفن أو خلاء في الصحراء يسع صفين . والخلاء في المسجد لا يمنع وإن وسع صفوفًا، لأن له حكم بقعة واحدة. واختلفوا في الحائل بينهما، والأصح الصحة إذا كان لا يشتبه عليه حال إمامه. المسافر إذا لم يقعد على رأس الركعتين فإنها تبطل إذا نوى الإقامة قبل أن يقيد الثالثة بسجدة. الأسير إذا خلص يقضي صلاة المقيمين إلا إذ رحل العدوّ به إلى مكان أراد الإقامة في خمسة عشر يوما فيقضيها صلاة المسافرين ولمن به شقيقة برأسه الإيماء. لو كان المريض بحال لو خرج إلى الجماعة لا يقدر على القيام ولو صلّى في بيته قدر عليه، الأصح أنه يخرج ويصلّي قاعدًا لأن الفرض مقدر بحاله على الاقتداء وعلى اعتباره سقط القيام واختلفوا في مريض إن قام لا يقدر على مراعاة سُنَّة القراءة، وإن قعد قدر الأصح أنه يقعد ويراعيها قدر المريض على بعض القيام قام بقدره. إذا كرر آية سجدة واحدة في مجلس واحد فالأفضل الاكتفاء بسجدة واحدة، وإذا كرّر اسم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فالأفضل تكرار الصلاة عليه وإن كفاه واحدة فيهما، ولا يرفع يديه في سجود التلاوة ولا فدية لسجود التلاوة ولا تجب نيَّة التعيين لها، والسنة القيام لها. إذا قرأ الإمام آية سجدة فالأفضل الركوع لها إن كان في صلاة المخافتة وإلا سجد لها. يُكرَه ترك السورة في الأخريين من التطوّع عمدا، وإن سها فعليه السهو، ولو ضمها في أخرى الفرض ساهيًا لا يسجد وعليه الفتوى لا يجوز الاقتداء بالشافعي في الوتر ) وإن كان لا يقطعه القرآن يخرج عن القرآنية بقصد الثناء؛ فلو قرأ الجُنُب الفاتحة بقصد الثناء لم يحرم ولو قصد بها الثناء في الجنازة لم يُكره إلا إذا قرأ المصلي قاصدًا الثناء فإنها تجزيه. لا رياء في الفرائض في حق سقوطها. إذا أراد فعل طاعة وخاف الرياء لا يتركها قراءة الفاتحة لأجل الممات عقب المكتوبة بدعة.
(1)
قال الشيخ محمد علي الطرابلسي في تعليقاته ص ٨٥ : (هذا) ضعيف، والصحيح الاقتداء به في الوتر إن لم يسلم على رأس الركعتين، وعدم الصحة إن سلم وقيل يصح الاقتداء، وإن سلم، ولا يضر كون الوتر سُنَّة عند الشافعي، وعند الحنفي واجبًا لأن اعتقاد الوجوب ليس بواجب على الحنفي، ومنه يعلم خطأ من اعتقد فساد اقتداء الحنفي بالشافعي في صلاة العيدين محتجا بأنه اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل لما ذكر).
·
القراءة في الحمام جهرًا مكروه وسرًا لا وهو المختار ولا يُكره للمحدث من كتب الفقه والحديث على الأصح وضع المقلمة على الكتاب مكروه إلا لأجل الكتابة، وضع المصحف تحت رأسه مكروه إلا للحفظ لا ينبغي تأقيت الدعاء إلا في الصلاة. يُكره الاقتداء في صلاة الرغائب وصلاة البراءة وليلة القدر، إلا إذا قال نذرت كذا ركعة بهذا الإمام بالجماعة كذا في البزازية. تعدّد السهو لا يُوجب تعدّد السجود إلا في المسبوق. يُكرَه الأذان قاعدًا إلا لنفسه الإسفار بالفجر أفضل إلا بمزدلفة للحاج. تأخير المغرب مكروه إلا في السفر أو على مائدة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم .
It is disliked not to arrange between surahs except in supererogatory prayer. Shortening recitation in the sunnah of Fajr is better than lengthening it. His nadhr supererogatory prayer is better – and it is said not. Speech between the sunnah and fard does not invalidate it, but decreases reward. It is disliked to designate a specific place in the mosque for his prayer; if he does so and someone else precedes him, he should not disturb him. He becomes started with the takbir unless he intends amazement rather than magnification. If the praying person reflects on other than his prayer, like his trade or study, it does not invalidate. If concerns distract him from his khushu‘, his reward is not diminished if it is not due to negligence; nor is it recommended to repeat it for leaving khushu‘. It is not befitting for the mu’adhdhin and imam to wait for anyone unless he is malicious. A man’s following one who is praying is valid even if he did not intend him to be imam; a woman’s following is not valid unless he intended her imamah except in Jumu‘ah and the two ‘Eids; and his intention of imamah for them is valid in their absence. The khatib after his commencement in supererogatory prayer cuts off at the end of two rak‘ahs unless in the sunnah of Jumu‘ah, then he completes it according to the sound view. He finds only a silk garment: he prays in it with no choice, unlike a najis garment where he has a choice; if he finds only the two, he prays in silk. Following in the courtyard of the mosque is like in the mosque, so following is valid even if rows are not connected. The preventer is a road where a carriage passes, or a river where ships sail, or an empty space in the desert that accommodates two rows. But emptiness in the mosque is not a preventer even if it accommodates rows, because it has the ruling of one place. They disagreed about a barrier between them; the sound view is validity if his imam’s situation is not ambiguous to him. The traveler: if he did not sit at the end of two rak‘ahs, it becomes invalid if he intended residence before tying the third with a prostration. The captive: when he is freed, he prays the prayers of residents unless the enemy traveled with him to a place where he intended residence for fifteen days, then he prays them as traveler’s prayers. For one with migraine, he signals with his head. If the patient is such that if he goes out to congregation he cannot stand, but if he prays at home he can stand, the sound view is that he goes out and prays sitting, because the fard is estimated according to his situation; and upon that consideration, standing falls. They disagreed about a patient who, if he stands, cannot observe the sunnah of recitation, but if he sits he can – the sound view is that he sits and observes it. A patient who can partially stand stands according to his ability. If he repeats one prostration verse in one sitting, the best is to suffice with one prostration. If he repeats the Prophet’s name ﷺ, the best is to repeat the blessing upon him, though one suffices in both. He does not raise his hands in sujud al-tilawah, nor is there any fidyah for it, nor is specifying the intention obligatory for it; and the sunnah is to stand for it. If the imam recites a prostration verse, the best is to bow for it if in a silent prayer, otherwise he prostrates for it. It is disliked to intentionally leave the surah in the last two of supererogatory prayer; if he forgets, he must perform sahw. If he adds it in another fard inadvertently, he does not prostrate, and upon it is the fatwa: it is not permissible to follow the Shafi‘i in witr. And if it is not that the Qur’an is cut off, it becomes non-Qur’anic by the intention of praise. So if a junub recites al-Fatihah with the intention of praise, it is not haram. If he intends praise with it in janazah, it is not disliked. But if the praying person recites intending praise, it suffices him. There is no riya’ in obligatory acts with respect to their validity. If he intends to do an act of obedience and fears riya’, he should not abandon it. Reciting al-Fatihah for the deceased after the prescribed prayer is an innovation. (1) Al-Shaykh Muhammad ‘Ali al-Tarabulsi said in his commentaries p. 85: “This is weak; the correct is that it is permissible to follow him in witr if he did not give salams at end of two rak‘ahs; and if he gave salams, it is not valid – and it is said it is valid even if he gave salams. And it does not harm that witr is sunnah according to Shafi‘i and wajib according to Hanafi, because believing it wajib is not obligatory for the Hanafi. From this one knows the error of whoever believes the invalidity of a Hanafi following a Shafi‘i in the prayer of the two ‘Eids, arguing that it is the following of one performing fard by one performing nafl due to what was mentioned.” (new line) Recitation in the bathroom aloud is disliked; silently, it is not – and that is the chosen view. It is not disliked for the one with hadath to touch books of fiqh and hadith according to the sound view. Placing a pen case on the book is disliked except for the sake of writing. Placing the mushaf under the head is disliked except for memorization. It is not proper to specify a fixed time for du‘a’ except in prayer. It is disliked to follow in the prayer of Ragha’ib, and the prayer of Bara’ah, and Laylat al-Qadr, unless he says: “I vowed such-and-such rak‘ahs with this imam in congregation” as in al-Bazzaziyyah. Multiplicity of forgetfulness does not necessitate multiplicity of prostrations except for the masbuq. It is disliked to give adhan while sitting unless for oneself. Dawn light (isfar) is better except at Muzdalifah for the pilgrim. Delaying Maghrib is disliked except while traveling or upon a spread. And Allah Almighty knows best.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This long passage is a detailed collection of rasm rulings (fixed rules) for the mufti, covering many aspects of prayer and related matters. It begins by stating that it is disliked (makruh) not to arrange surahs in order of revelation in supererogatory prayers, except in nafl. Shortening recitation in Fajr sunnah is better than lengthening it. Vowed supererogatory prayers are superior – with disagreement. Speaking between sunnah and fard does not invalidate either, but reduces reward. Designating a fixed spot in the mosque for prayer is disliked; if someone else takes it, do not oust them. One becomes in prayer with the takbir unless the intention was pure amazement. Inner thoughts foreign to prayer (like trade or study) do not invalidate the prayer. Loss of khushu‘ due to worldly concerns does not reduce reward if not from negligence, and repeating such a prayer is not recommended. The mu’adhdhin and imam should not wait for latecomers except a troublesome person. A man can validly follow another man in prayer even if the latter did not intend to be imam; a woman cannot follow a man unless he intended her imamah – except in Jumu‘ah and ‘Eid prayers, where his intention of their imamah is valid even if they are absent. A khatib who starts a supererogatory prayer must cut it off after two rak’ahs, unless it is the sunnah of Jumu’ah (then he completes it). If only a silk garment is available, one must pray in it without choice (to cover); but if both a silk and a najis garment are available, one chooses between them. Following in the courtyard of the mosque is like following inside; gaps in rows do not invalidate as long as there is no major barrier like a wide road or river. Emptiness of rows within the mosque is not a barrier. A barrier (like a wall) between imam and follower: the soundest opinion is validity if the follower is not confused about the imam’s actions. A traveler who does not sit after two rak’ahs: if he intended residence before tying the third rak’ah, his prayer becomes invalid. A captive upon release prays as a resident unless he resided fifteen days in enemy territory. A migraine sufferer may signal. A patient who cannot stand in congregation but can stand at home should go to the mosque and pray sitting. A patient who can only observe correct recitation while sitting should sit. When repeating the same prostration verse in one sitting, one sufficing prostration is best; repeating the Prophet’s name likewise best with repeated blessings, though one suffices. Hands are not raised in sujud al-tilawah; no fidyah; specific intention for it is not obligatory; standing is sunnah. An imam in a silent prayer should bow for the prostration verse; otherwise, he prostrates. Deliberately omitting a surah in the last two rak’ahs of a nafl is disliked; if forgotten, sahw prostrations are required. Adding a surah in a fard after the second rak’ah inadvertently does not require sahw. The fatwa is that a Hanafi may not follow a Shafi‘i in witr (with a detailed footnote from Tarabulsi clarifying exceptions). A junub reciting Fatihah with the intention of praise is not haram. Intending praise in janazah is not disliked. Riya‘ does not affect validity of obligatory acts. If one fears riya’ in an act of obedience, do not abandon it. Reciting Fatihah for the deceased after fard is innovation. Then follow miscellaneous rulings: reciting aloud in bathroom disliked; silent recitation not disliked. Touching books of fiqh/hadith is not disliked for one in hadath. Placing a pen case on a book is disliked except for writing. Placing mushaf under head is disliked except for memorization. Fixing a time for du‘a‘ outside prayer is not proper. Following in innovated prayers (Ragha’ib, Bara’ah, Laylat al-Qadr) is disliked unless vowed. Multiple forgetfulness does not multiply sajw except for masbuq. Adhan while sitting disliked unless for oneself. Making Fajr dawn prayer early (isfar) is better except at Muzdalifah. Delaying Maghrib is disliked except when traveling or eating. And Allah knows best.

Key Terms
السهو (al-sahw): Forgetfulness in prayer; certain omissions require prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw).
المسبوق (al-masbūq): One who joins the prayer late (missed one or more rak'ahs).
الإسفار (al-isfār): Dawn light (making Fajr prayer at a later time when light is clear).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa in the passage, is it permissible for a Hanafi to follow a Shafi'i in witr prayer?
A) Yes, always
B) No, not permissible
C) Yes, but only if the Hanafi intends witr as sunnah
D) Yes, but only if the Shafi'i imam does not give salams after two rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
The fatwa prohibits following a Shafi'i in witr, but Tarabulsi's conditional permission reflects a minority view within the school.

The Faqih's Books and Zakat: When Necessity Meets Debt
Rasm rule: Zakat exemption for a faqih's books with exception for debts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a faqih's needed books are not zakatable wealth, and identify the exception for debts owed to people.

Core Idea
A faqih's books are exempt from zakat, but can be sold to repay debts.

This passage from 'Al-Ashbah wa al-Nadā'ir' presents a concise rasm rule concerning the zakat status of a jurist's books. In Hanafi fiqh, essential scholarly tools are not considered surplus wealth subject to zakat. However, the text introduces a critical exception: when the faqih owes a debt to another person, the exemption is overridden, and the books may be sold to satisfy that debt. This rule balances the protection of scholarly work with the obligation to repay debts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The faqih is not considered wealthy (ghani) by his needed books – i.e., he is not required to pay zakat on them.
2
Locate the exception
The phrase 'illa fi dayn al-‘ibad' (except in debts of people) signals the only case where the rule is overridden.
3
Understand the consequence
In the exceptional case, the books are sold to repay the debt (tuba' li-qada' al-dayn).
The books are not immune from sale; they can be taken by the creditor.
4
Reflect on the rationale
The rule protects essential tools for learning and teaching, but the claim of another person's debt takes precedence because it is a right of a human being (haqq adami).
This reflects the Hanafi prioritization of huquq al-‘ibad over huquq Allah in this context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة
الفقيه لا يكون غنيا بكتبه المحتاج إليها إلا في دين العباد، فتباع لقضاء الدين؛ كذا في منظومة ابن وهبان الاعتبار لوزن مكة. مَن له دين على مفلس مقرّ فقير على
Book of Zakat. The faqih is not considered wealthy by his books that he needs, except with respect to debts of people; so they are sold to repay the debt. Thus in the poem of Ibn Wahban: 'Al-I'tibar li-Wazni Makkah'. Whoever has a debt upon an insolvent person who acknowledges a poor person upon...
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This short passage begins a new section on zakat. It states a rasm rule: a scholar (faqih) is not considered wealthy (ghani) for zakat purposes by virtue of his books if they are books he needs, meaning he does not have to pay zakat on them because they are essential for his work. However, there is an exception concerning debts owed to people (duyun al-‘ibad): if he owes a debt to someone, his books can be sold to repay that debt, even though they are not considered excess wealth for zakat. The passage cites the book 'Al-I'tibar li-Wazni Makkah' by Ibn Wahban. The text then begins another rule about a person who has a debt on an insolvent person who acknowledges a poor person, but it cuts off. The incomplete sentence likely continues the discussion on zakat and debts.

Key Terms
الفقيه (al-faqīh): A scholar of fiqh; a jurist who needs books for his work and study.
دين العباد (dayn al-‘ibād): Debts owed to people (as opposed to rights of Allah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, under what condition can a faqih's books be sold?
A) To pay zakat on them
B) To repay a debt owed to people
C) To give charity
D) They can never be sold

Key Takeaway
A faqih's needed books are exempt from zakat but may be sold to repay personal debts.

Sick Person's Prayer Sitting: The Maxim of Obligation Scaled by Ability
Ruling on sick person's prayer sitting based on maxim of obligation scaled to ability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-fard muqaddar bi-halih' to a sick person's prayer scenario and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Obligation is measured by ability; when standing harms Sunnah recitation, sitting is preferred.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi qawida: 'al-fard muqaddar bi-halih' (the obligation is measured by one's condition). The text applies it to a sick person who can stand but cannot properly perform the Sunnah recitation. You will see how scholars differed on the priority of standing versus recitation, and why the sound opinion (al-asahh) opts for sitting to preserve the recitation. Understanding this maxim helps in deriving rulings for similar situations where ability is compromised.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its scope
Identify the qawida: 'al-fard muqaddar bi-halih'. Understand that it governs acts of worship when full performance is not possible. The obligation adjusts to the person's state and ability.
This is a sughra (minor) maxim, but widely applied in ibadat.
2
Identify the case and the conflict
The case is a sick person who can stand but by doing so cannot observe the Sunnah recitation (proper tilawah). The conflict is between the obligation to stand and the Sunnah of recitation.
Sunnah recitation here refers to the recommended manner, not the wajib recitation itself.
3
Apply the maxim to the case
The maxim says the obligation (standing) is scaled by ability. Since standing prevents fulfilling the Sunnah recitation, the obligation of standing is reduced, allowing sitting to preserve the recitation. The ruling: he sits.
The qawida overrides the default priority of standing because of the conflicting Sunnah.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf
Some scholars argued that standing as a rukn (pillar) should take precedence. The response uses the maxim to show that the Sunnah of recitation is also important, and the obligation is scaled down.
The tarjih (preference) is given to the sound opinion (al-asahh) that he sits.
5
Extract the fatwa ruling
The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is that the sick person sits and recites properly. If he can stand partially, he does so. This demonstrates the practical application of the maxim in fatwa.
This is a clear example of how qawaid guide fatwa in cases of conflicting considerations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنه يخرج ويصلّي قاعدًا لأن الفرض مقدر بحاله على الاقتداء وعلى اعتباره سقط القيام واختلفوا في مريض إن قام لا يقدر على مراعاة سُنَّة القراءة، وإن قعد قدر الأصح أنه يقعد ويراعيها قدر المريض على بعض القيام قام بقدره.
That he goes out and prays sitting because the obligation is measured by his condition; by considering that, standing is dropped. And they differed concerning a sick person: if he stands, he cannot observe the Sunnah of recitation; and if he sits, he can. The sound opinion is that he sits and observes it. The sick person who can manage some standing does so according to his ability.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage applies the qawida (legal maxim) 'الفرض مقدر بحاله' (the obligation is measured by one's condition) to a specific case. The ruling is about a sick person who can stand but cannot perform the Sunnah recitation properly while standing. By the maxim, the obligation of standing is dropped, and he sits to preserve the Sunnah recitation. The text notes an ikhtilaf (disagreement) among scholars: the sound (asahh) opinion is that he sits. The principle also applies to one who can stand partially—he stands as much as he is able.

Key Terms
الفرض مقدر بحاله (al-fard muqaddar bi-halih): The obligatory act is scaled to the person's state and ability
سنة القراءة (sunnat al-qira'ah): The recommended manner of recitation in prayer (not the obligation to recite)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what should a sick person do if he can stand but cannot properly observe the Sunnah of recitation?
A) Stand anyway, since standing is obligatory.
B) Sit to preserve the Sunnah recitation.
C) Skip recitation and stand.
D) Perform the prayer lying down.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'al-fard muqaddar bi-halih' obligates scaling down acts of worship when full performance is impossible or harms another Sunnah; in doubt, the sound opinion preserves the more essential Sunnah.

Repeating Sajdah Tilawah and Salawat in One Gathering
Ruling on repetition of prostration verse and Prophet's name in one gathering

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the preferred (afdal) ruling when a prostration verse or the Prophet's name is repeated in one gathering, and apply the principle that a single performance suffices.

Core Idea
One prostration suffices for repeated recitation; one salawat suffices for repeated name, though repeating salawat is better.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair lays down a key practical maxim: repetition of the same cause in one gathering does not multiply the required response. Yet, for the Prophet's name, the optimum is to repeat the blessing each time. Understanding this distinction is essential for issuing correct fatwas on daily recitation practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the repeated element
Determine whether the repetition involves a verse of prostration or the name of the Prophet (PBUH). The ruling differs slightly.
The same principle of sufficiency applies to both, but the preferred action varies.
2
Apply the general rule of sufficiency
In both cases, a single act – one prostration or one salutation – suffices for all repetitions in the same gathering.
The text explicitly says 'وإن كفاه واحدة فيهما' – one suffices in both.
3
Note the preferential ruling (afdal)
For sajdah, the afdal is to suffice with one prostration. For the Prophet's name, the afdal is to repeat the salawat each time.
The difference lies in the nature of the act: one is physical, the other verbal.
4
Understand the rationale
The gathering (majlis) unites the repeated acts; the cause is the same, so the obligation is not multiplied.
This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that multiple occurrences of a cause in one session do not require multiple responses.
5
Distinguish from multiple gatherings
If the repetitions occur in separate gatherings, each gathering requires its own act. The rule only applies within one majlis.
The text specifies 'في مجلس واحد' – in one sitting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا كرر آية سجدة واحدة في مجلس واحد فالأفضل الاكتفاء بسجدة واحدة، وإذا كرّر اسم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فالأفضل تكرار الصلاة عليه وإن كفاه واحدة فيهما، ولا يرفع يديه في سجود التلاوة ولا فدية لسجود التلاوة ولا تجب نيَّة التعيين لها، والسنة القيام لها. إذا قرأ الإمام آية سجدة فالأفضل الركوع لها إن كان في صلاة المخافتة وإلا سجد لها.
If one repeats a single verse of prostration in one sitting, the best is to suffice with one prostration. If one repeats the name of the Prophet (peace be upon him), the best is to repeat the salutation upon him, though one suffices in both. One does not raise the hands in sajdah tilawah, nor is there a ransom (fidya) for it, nor is the specific intention (niyyat al-ta'yin) required; and it is sunnah to stand for it. If the imam recites a prostration verse, the best is to bow (ruku) for it if in a silent prayer, otherwise he prostrates for it.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage collects several rulings (rasm) concerning sajdah tilawah (prostration of recitation) and sending salawat upon the Prophet (PBUH). The key points: 1) If you repeat a prostration verse multiple times in the same gathering, one prostration suffices and is preferable. 2) If you repeat the Prophet's name, it is better to repeat the salawat each time, though one is enough. 3) For sajdah tilawah: do not raise hands, no fidya, intention of a specific prostration is not obligatory, and it is sunnah to perform it standing. 4) If the imam recites a prostration verse in a silent prayer, he should make ruku (bowing) as his prostration; otherwise, he prostrates. These are rules of practice, not derived from a single maxim.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration
نية التعيين (niyyat al-ta'yin): Specific intention to perform a particular prostration (e.g., for a specific verse)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the best (afdal) action when a person repeats a prostration verse multiple times in one gathering?
A) Perform a prostration for each repetition
B) Suffice with one prostration
C) Make two prostrations
D) Do nothing

Key Takeaway
When the cause repeats in one gathering, one act suffices, but for the Prophet's name, repeating salawat is preferable.

Specific Rulings of Sajdah Tilawah
Specific rulings of sajdah tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific rulings of sajdah tilawah regarding raising hands, fidya, intention, standing, and the imam's action in prayer.

Core Idea
Sajdah tilawah has unique rules: no hand raising, no fidya, no specific intention; sunnah to stand; imam bows in silent prayer.

This passage continues with a list of distinct rules for sajdah tilawah that a mufti must know when advising on prayer and recitation. These rules are based on the nature of sajdah tilawah as a wajib act with simplified conditions.

Guided Path
1
List the prohibitions
Identify what is explicitly negated: no raising of hands, no fidya (ransom), and no requirement of a specific intention (niyyat al-ta'yin).
These simplify the act, distinguishing it from regular prayer.
2
Note the sunnah
It is sunnah (recommended) to stand while performing sajdah tilawah.
Standing is not obligatory but enhances the act.
3
Identify the imam's scenario
When the imam recites a prostration verse during prayer, the afdal action depends on whether the prayer is silent (mukhafatah) or loud (jahr).
In silent prayers, bowing (ruku) with the intention of sajdah tilawah is afdal; in loud prayers, actual prostration is afdal.
4
Understand the reason for the distinction
In silent prayers, the ruku is less disruptive and can serve as the prostration; in loud prayers, the prostration is more fitting.
The ruling aims for ease and practicality.
