The Maxim: No Riya in Obligatory Acts Regarding Validity
A maxim and its furuat from Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'لا رياء في الفرائض في حق سقوطها' to distinguish the validity of obligatory versus voluntary acts when riya is present.

Core Idea
Obligatory acts are valid even with ostentation; voluntary acts may be invalidated.

This lesson explores a foundational maxim from Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir that clarifies the effect of ostentation on the validity of acts of worship. The maxim states that riya does not affect the validity of obligatory acts—meaning the act is legally valid, though sin is incurred. However, this protection does not extend to voluntary acts. Understanding this distinction is essential for issuing correct fatwas on acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act as obligatory or voluntary
Determine if the act in question is a fard (obligatory) or nafl (voluntary). The maxim only applies to fard.
2
Assess the presence and nature of riya
Riya can be the sole motive or mixed. The maxim means that even if riya is present, the obligatory act is valid (sahih), though the reward may be lost and sin incurred.
This is in contrast to voluntary acts where riya can invalidate the act.
3
Apply the maxim to the furuat in the text
The passage gives examples: reciting al-Fatihah intending praise (not Quranic recitation) suffices for the worshipper. Similarly, a junub reciting with intention of praise is not forbidden. These cases show the maxim in action.
4
Distinguish from voluntary acts and note limitations
For voluntary acts, riya can render the act invalid. The maxim is restricted to 'fara'id' and does not apply to nafl or supererogatory acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يُكرَه ترك السورة في الأخريين من التطوّع عمدا، وإن سها فعليه السهو، ولو ضمها في أخرى الفرض ساهيًا لا يسجد وعليه الفتوى لا يجوز الاقتداء بالشافعي في الوتر ) وإن كان لا يقطعه القرآن يخرج عن القرآنية بقصد الثناء؛ فلو قرأ الجُنُب الفاتحة بقصد الثناء لم يحرم ولو قصد بها الثناء في الجنازة لم يُكره إلا إذا قرأ المصلي قاصدًا الثناء فإنها تجزيه. لا رياء في الفرائض في حق سقوطها. إذا أراد فعل طاعة وخاف الرياء لا يتركها قراءة الفاتحة لأجل الممات عقب المكتوبة بدعة. (1) · القراءة في الحمام جهرًا مكروه وسرًا لا وهو المختار ولا يُكره للمحدث من كتب الفقه والحديث على الأصح وضع المقلمة على الكتاب مكروه إلا لأجل الكتابة، وضع المصحف تحت رأسه مكروه إلا للحفظ لا ينبغي تأقيت الدعاء إلا في الصلاة. يُكره الاقتداء في صلاة الرغائب وصلاة البراءة وليلة القدر، إلا إذا قال نذرت كذا ركعة بهذا الإمام بالجماعة كذا في البزازية. تعدّد السهو لا يُوجب تعدّد السجود إلا في المسبوق. يُكرَه الأذان قاعدًا إلا لنفسه الإسفار بالفجر أفضل إلا بمزدلفة للحاج. تأخير المغرب مكروه إلا في السفر أو على مائدة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم .
It is makruh to intentionally omit the surah in the last two rak'ahs of voluntary prayer. If one forgets, then prostrations of forgetfulness are due. If one inadvertently adds (a surah) in another (rak'ah) of obligatory prayer, no prostration is required; the fatwa is on this. It is not permissible to follow a Shafi'i imam in Witr. And if (the recitation) does not separate from the Qur'an by intending praise—so if a junub recites al-Fatihah intending praise, it is not forbidden; and if he intends praise in funeral prayer, it is not makruh; but if the worshipper recites intending praise, it suffices him. There is no ostentation (riya) in obligatory acts regarding their validity. If one wants to perform an act of obedience and fears ostentation, he should not abandon it. Reciting al-Fatihah for the deceased after the obligatory prayer is innovation. (1) Recitation aloud in the bathroom is makruh; silently is not, and that is the chosen opinion. It is not makruh for a person in minor impurity to touch books of fiqh and hadith, according to the sound opinion. Placing a pen case on a book is makruh except for writing. Placing the Quran under the head is makruh except for preservation. It is not proper to fix a specific time for supplication except in prayer. It is makruh to follow in the prayers of Ragha'ib, Bara'ah, and Laylat al-Qadr, unless one says, 'I have vowed such rak'ahs with this imam in congregation,' as in al-Bazzaziyyah. Multiple forgetfulness does not necessitate multiple prostrations except for a latecomer (masbuq). It is makruh to give the adhan while sitting except for oneself. Performing Fajr in darkness is best except at Muzdalifah for the pilgrim. Delaying Maghrib is makruh except when traveling or at a meal. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage compiles numerous rulings (ahkam) on makruh (disliked) acts and specific issues. The primary maxim here is 'لا رياء في الفرائض في حق سقوطها' (There is no ostentation in obligatory acts regarding their validity), which means that if one performs an obligatory act with even a hint of showing off, the act is still valid, though sinful. This is applied to the case of a worshipper reciting al-Fatihah intending praise: it suffices. The passage also addresses the impermissibility of following a Shafi'i imam in Witr (the footnote clarifies exceptions). Many specific makruh rulings are listed, such as reciting aloud in bathroom, placing a pen case on a book, etc. The underlying logic often relates to respect for the Quran and prayer.

Key Terms
الرياء (al-riya): Ostentation, performing an act to be seen by others

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the maxim, if a person prays Fajr with ostentation, the prayer is:
A) Invalid
B) Valid but sinful
C) Valid and rewarded
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'لا رياء في الفرائض في حق سقوطها' ensures that obligatory acts remain valid despite ostentation, preserving their legal effect while holding the person accountable for the sin.

Following a Shafi'i Imam in Witr and Key Makruh Rulings for the Mufti
A dispute on following Shafi'i in Witr and a collection of makruh rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on following a Shafi'i imam in Witr and identify the relied-upon fatwa, and list three makruh acts from the passage related to Islamic etiquette.

Core Idea
It is not permissible for a Hanafi to follow a Shafi'i imam in Witr; other makruh rulings preserve the sanctity of worship and knowledge.

This lesson examines a critical fatwa issue: can a Hanafi follower pray Witr behind a Shafi'i imam? The Hanafi school generally prohibits this because Witr is wajib for Hanafis but sunnah for Shafi'is, leading to a mismatch in intention and validity. The passage also lists several makruh acts, including reciting aloud in the bathroom, placing a pen case on a book, and placing the Quran under the head. These rulings reflect the high regard for the Quran and proper conduct (adab) in Islamic practice.

Guided Path
1
Understand the nature of Witr in Hanafi and Shafi'i schools
Witr is wajib (obligatory) in Hanafi and sunnah (recommended) in Shafi'i. This difference affects the validity of following an imam.
2
Analyze the ruling in the passage
The text says 'لا يجوز الاقتداء بالشافعي في الوتر' (It is not permissible). The relied-upon fatwa (al-mukhtar) is impermissibility.
Some later Hanafis allowed it conditionally, but the text sides with impermissibility.
3
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
A Hanafi should not pray Witr behind a Shafi'i unless the Shafi'i imam does not shorten it (i.e., prays three rak'ahs without taslim after two).
4
Examine the makruh rulings related to adab
The passage lists actions like reciting aloud in the bathroom (makruh), placing a pen case on a book (makruh except for writing), and placing Quran under head (makruh except for preservation). These show the respect required for books and Quran.
5
Apply the rule about multiple sahw
The masbuq (latecomer) has special rules: multiple forgetfulness does not require multiple prostrations except for the masbuq.

Source Text

Zakah and Fitrana: The Two Capabilities
A collection of rulings grounded in a single qawida

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida on zakah vs fitrana capability types to determine lapse of obligation and state the mufta bihi on forcible collection of zakah.

Core Idea
Zakah lapses if wealth is lost; fitrana persists because its obligation is based on possible capability, not actual possession.

A mufti must understand the precise conditions under which wealth-based obligations lapse. This lesson unpacks a key qawida from the Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir that contrasts the capabilities required for zakah and sadaqat al-fitr. Mastery of this distinction prevents errors in fatwa on pending obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Obligations
Locate the qawida: 'الزكاة واجبة بقدرة ميسرة... وصدقة الفطر واجبة بقدرة ممكنة'. Note that zakah and fitrana are classified differently.
The qawida is placed at the end of the passage but governs many earlier details.
2
Understand the Two Capabilities
Define 'qudrah muyassarah' (easily accessible wealth) vs 'qudrah mumkinah' (possible capability, including ability to earn). The first requires actual possession; the second only the possibility at the time of obligation.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi fiqh and has practical consequences.
3
Apply to the Given Furuat
Work through the two furuat: (a) wealth destroyed after the year → no zakah due; (b) person becomes poor after Eid day → fitrana still wajib. Check consistency with the qawida.
Other rulings in the text (e.g., on depositing money) also reflect this principle.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf on Forcible Collection
Examine the dispute: some say zakah can be taken forcibly from a refuser; the mu'tamad says no. Understand the reasoning and the thamarah (the judge may imprison but not take forcefully).
This is an example of tarjih within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة
الفقيه لا يكون غنيا بكتبه المحتاج إليها إلا في دين العباد، فتباع لقضاء الدين؛ كذا في منظومة ابن وهبان الاعتبار لوزن مكة. مَن له دين على مفلس مقرّ فقير على المختار. المريض مرض الموت إذا دفع زكاته إلى أخته ثم مات وهي وارثته أجزأته وقعت موقعها؛ فإن كان له وارث آخر ردت لأنه لا وصية لوارث تصدق بطعام الغير عن صدقة فطره توقف على إجازته ؛ فإن أجاز بشرائطها وضمنه جازت. المأمور بدفع الزكاة إذا تصدق بدراهم نفسه أجزأه إن كان على نية الرجوع وكانت دراهم المأمور قائمة.
نوى الزكاة إلا أنه سماه قرضًا اختلفوا، والصحيح الجواز.
عبد الخدمة إذا أذِنَ له في التجارة لا يكون للتجارة فتجب صدقة فطره
• عين الناذر مسكينًا فله إعطاء غيره إلا إذا لم يعين المنذور ؛ كما لو قال الله عليَّ أن أطعم هذا المسكين شيئًا فإنه يتعيَّن، ولو عيَّن مسكينين له الاقتصار على واحد يحبس الممتنع عن أداء الزكاة، واختلفوا في أخذها منه جبرًا والمعتمد لا. حول الزكاة قمري لا شمسي كل الصدقات حرام على بني هاشم زكاة أو عمالة فيها أو عشرًا أو كفَّارة أو منذورة إلا التطوع والوقف. شك أنه أدى الزكاة أم لا؛ فإنه يؤديها
لأن وقتها العمر.
أودع مالاً ونسيه ثم تذكره لم تجب الزكاة إلا إذا كان المودع من المعارف. دين العباد مانع من وجوبها إلا المهر المؤجل إذا كان الزوج لا يريد أداءه. يُكره إعطاء نصاب لفقير منها إلا إذا كان مديونا أو صاحب عيال؛ لو فرقه عليهم لم يخص كلاً منهم نصاب .
يُكرَه نقلها إلا إلى قرابة أو أحوج، أو من دار الحرب إلى دار الإسلام، أو إلى طالب علم ، أو إلى الزهاد، أو كانت زكاة معجّلة .
المختار أنه لا يجوز دفع الزكاة لأهل البدع. دفعها لأخته المتزوجة إن كان زوجها معسرًا جاز، وإن كان موسرًا وكان مهرها أقل من النصاب فكذلك، وإن كان المعجل قدره لم يجز وبه يفتي وكذا في لزوم الأضحية .
الولد من الزنا لا يثبت نسبه من الزاني في شيء إلا في الشهادة، لا تقبل للزاني، وفي الزكاة، لا يجوز دفع زكاة الزاني إلى الولد من الزنا إلا إذا كان من امرأة لها زوج معروف كما في جامع الفصولين.
الزكاة واجبة بقدرة ميسرة فتسقط بهلاك المال بعد الحول وصدقة الفطر واجبة بقدرة ممكنة، فلو افتقر بعد يوم العيد لم تسقط .
Book of Zakah. The jurist is not considered wealthy by his needed books except regarding the debts of people; so they are sold to repay debts; thus in the poem of Ibn Wahban. The consideration is by Meccan weight. One who has a debt upon an insolvent person who admits [the debt] is poor, according to the chosen opinion. A person terminally ill who pays his zakah to his sister, then dies and she is his heir, it suffices him and falls in its place; but if he has another heir, it is returned because there is no bequest to an heir. One gives charity of another's food for his fitr sadaqah, it depends on his permission; if he permits with its conditions and guarantees it, it is valid. The one ordered to pay zakah, if he gives charity from his own dirhams, it suffices him if he intended to reclaim it and the dirhams of the one ordered were extant. He intended zakah but called it a loan: they differed; the correct is permissibility. A service slave, if given permission to trade, is not considered a trader, so his fitr sadaqah is obligatory. The one who vows specifies a poor person: he may give to another unless he did not specify the vowed, as if he said: 'Upon me is to feed this poor person something' then it becomes specified. If he specifies two poor persons, he may confine to one. One who refuses to pay zakah is imprisoned; they differed about taking it from him forcibly, and the relied-upon is no. The zakah year is lunar, not solar. All charities are forbidden to Banu Hashim: zakah, wages therein, tithe, expiation, or vowed charity except voluntary charity and endowment. If one doubts whether he paid zakah or not, he pays it because its time is one's entire life. If one deposits money and forgets it, then remembers, zakah is not due unless the depositor is among those known. Debts of people prevent its obligation except the deferred dower if the husband does not intend to pay it. It is makruh to give a full nisab to one poor person from it unless he is in debt or has a family; if he distributes it among them, he does not assign each a full nisab. It is makruh to transfer it except to relatives or more needy, or from dar al-harb to dar al-Islam, or to a student of knowledge, or to the ascetics, or if it is expedited zakah. The chosen is that it is not permissible to pay zakah to people of innovation. Paying it to his married sister: if her husband is insolvent, it is permissible; if he is wealthy and her dowry is less than nisab, similarly; if the expedited amount equals nisab, it is not permissible, and fatwa is upon this; similarly for the obligation of sacrifice. The child of zina does not have his lineage established from the adulterer in anything except in testimony; it is not accepted for the adulterer; and in zakah, it is not permissible to pay zakah of the adulterer to the child of zina unless from a woman with a known husband, as in Jami' al-Fusulayn. Zakah is obligatory with facilitated capability, so it lapses if wealth perishes after the year; but sadaqat al-fitr is obligatory with possible capability, so if one becomes poor after the day of Eid, it does not lapse.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Zakah lists numerous detailed rulings (ahkam) that are applications of several Hanafi qawaid (legal maxims). The opening maxim is stated at the end: 'الزكاة واجبة بقدرة ميسرة' (Zakah is obligatory with facilitated capability) as opposed to fitr sadaqah which is 'ممكنة' (possible capability). Key applications include: a jurist's books are not counted as wealth for zakah but are sold for debt. A terminally ill person paying zakah to an heir is valid only if no other heirs (since it's a bequest). The qawida 'المشقة تجلب التيسير' is applied in rulings like doubting payment: pay again because doubt does not remove certainty. Rulings on prohibited recipients (Banu Hashim, people of innovation, child of zina under conditions) derive from textual evidence. The passage demonstrates how the Hanafi school meticulously conditions zakah obligations and transfers.

Key Terms
قدرة ميسرة (qudrah muyassarah): Capability that is easily accessible (e.g., wealth present and accessible for a year)
قدرة ممكنة (qudrah mumkinah): Capability that is possible (includes earning capacity)
بني هاشم (Bani Hashim): Descendants of Hashim (the Prophet's clan)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the qawida in this passage, what is the status of fitrana if a person becomes poor on the 2nd of Shawwal (after Eid day)?
A) The obligation lapses because he has no wealth.
B) The obligation remains because fitrana is based on possible capability (qudrah mumkinah).
C) The obligation is suspended until he regains wealth.
D) The obligation transforms into a debt on his estate.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes zakah from fitrana by the type of capability required, leading to different rulings on lapse: zakah lapses if wealth perishes after the year; fitrana persists even if poverty strikes after Eid.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
12 min
Parsing Fatwa Rulings on Zakah: A Rasm al-Mufti Exercise
Collection of fatwa rulings on zakah cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the muftā bihī position for each specific zakah scenario in the passage and apply the underlying maxims to similar cases.

Core Idea
Zakah rulings are case-specific: the same act may be valid or invalid depending on the giver, receiver, and circumstances.

This passage presents a series of fatwa rulings on zakah, each addressing a distinct scenario. The rulings are drawn from the Hanafi madhhab's relied-upon positions (al-mukhtār). Your task is to parse each ruling, identify the operative legal maxim or condition, and understand how the muftī arrives at the conclusion. This parsing exercise will sharpen your ability to apply qawāʿid to practical cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific case
Read each sentence and determine the subject (who is acting) and the object (what is being done). For example: a terminally ill person paying zakah to his sister who is his heir.
Pay attention to the condition (e.g., 'if he has another heir' or 'if her husband is poor').
2
Extract the ruling
Determine whether the act is valid (jāʾiz), invalid (ghayr jāʾiz), disliked (makrūh), or contingent. Note the use of terms like 'ajzaʾa' (suffices) or 'lā yajūz' (not permissible).
If there is a difference of opinion, the text often states 'al-mukhtār' or 'wa bihi yuftā' to indicate the operative view.
3
Identify the underlying principle or maxim
Link the ruling to a general fiqh principle. For example: 'no bequest to an heir' explains why payment to an heir with other heirs is invalid as a bequest. Another principle: 'zakah is lifted by destruction after the year' shows the condition of ability.
Some rulings are based on the status of the recipient (e.g., Banu Hashim, innovators, students) or the nature of the payment (lunar year, debt, etc.).
4
Note the authority level
Determine whether the ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, al-mukhtār, or a later fatwa. The passage often uses 'al-mukhtār' to signal the relied-upon position.
If the text says 'ikhtalafū' and then 'al-muʿtamad lā', the latter is the position for fatwa.
5
Apply to a similar scenario
Take one ruling and change a variable (e.g., different relative, different timing) and reason whether the ruling would change. This tests your understanding of the operative condition.
For example: if a wealthy person gives zakah to his poor brother, it is allowed; but if the brother is an heir and there are other heirs, it may be invalid as a bequest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المختار. المريض مرض الموت إذا دفع زكاته إلى أخته ثم مات وهي وارثته أجزأته ووقعت موقعها؛ فإن كان له وارث آخر ردّت لأنه لا وصية لوارث تصدق بطعام الغير عن صدقة فطره توقف على إجازته ؛ فإن أجاز بشرائطها وضمنه جازت. المأمور بدفع الزكاة إذا تصدق بدراهم نفسه أجزأه إن كان على نية الرجوع وكانت دراهم المأمور قائمة. نوى الزكاة إلا أنه سماه قرضًا اختلفوا، والصحيح الجواز. عبد الخدمة إذا أذِنَ له في التجارة لا يكون للتجارة فتجب صدقة فطره • عين الناذر مسكينًا فله إعطاء غيره إلا إذا لم يعين المنذور ؛ كما لو قال الله عليَّ أن أطعم هذا المسكين شيئًا فإنه يتعيَّن، ولو عيَّن مسكينين له الاقتصار على واحد يحبس الممتنع عن أداء الزكاة، واختلفوا في أخذها منه جبرًا والمعتمد لا. حول الزكاة قمري لا شمسي كل الصدقات حرام على بني هاشم زكاة أو عمالة فيها أو عشرًا أو كفَّارة أو منذورة إلا التطوع والوقف. شك أنه أدى الزكاة أم لا؛ فإنه يؤديها لأن وقتها العمر. أودع مالاً ونسيه ثم تذكره لم تجب الزكاة إلا إذا كان المودع من المعارف. دين العباد مانع من وجوبها إلا المهر المؤجل إذا كان الزوج لا يريد أداءه. يُكره إعطاء نصاب لفقير منها إلا إذا كان مديونا أو صاحب عيال؛ لو فرقه عليهم لم يخص كلاً منهم نصاب . يُكرَه نقلها إلا إلى قرابة أو أحوج، أو من دار الحرب إلى دار الإسلام، أو إلى طالب علم ، أو إلى الزهاد، أو كانت زكاة معجّلة . المختار أنه لا يجوز دفع الزكاة لأهل البدع. دفعها لأخته المتزوجة إن كان زوجها معسرًا جاز، وإن كان موسرًا وكان مهرها أقل من النصاب فكذلك، وإن كان المعجل قدره لم يجز وبه يفتي وكذا في لزوم الأضحية . الولد من الزنا لا يثبت نسبه من الزاني في شيء إلا في الشهادة، لا تقبل للزاني، وفي الزكاة، لا يجوز دفع زكاة الزاني إلى الولد من الزنا إلا إذا كان من امرأة لها زوج معروف كما في جامع الفصولين. الزكاة واجبة بقدرة ميسرة فتسقط بهلاك المال بعد الحول وصدقة الفطر واجبة بقدرة ممكنة، فلو افتقر بعد يوم العيد لم تسقط . ١٤٢ أنفق على أقاربه بنيَّة الزكاة جاز إلا إذا حكم عليه بنفقتهم، وتحلّ الصدقة لمن له غلة عقار لا تكفيه وعياله سنة، ومن معه ألف وعليه مثلها كره له الأخذ وأجزأ الدافع، ولو له قوت سنة يساوي نصابا أو كسوة شتوية لا يحتاج إليها في الصيف، فالصحيح حلّ الأخذ . عجلها عن نصاب عنده فتم الحول وعنده أقل من النصاب؛ إن دفعها إلى الفقير لا يستردّها مطلقا، وإلى الساعي يستردّها إن كانت قائمة وإن قسمها الساعي بين الفقراء ضمنها من مال الزكاة خلافًا لمحمد، ولو عجّل زكاة حمل السوائم بعد وجوده جاز لا قبله. وفي الملتقط من الإجارة : المعلم إذا أعطى خليفته شيئًا ناويا الزكاة؛ فإن كان بحيث يعمل له لو لم يعطه يصح عنها وإلا فلا.
The chosen [position]. A terminally ill person who pays his zakah to his sister, then dies while she is his heir, it suffices and falls in its place; but if he has another heir, it is returned because there is no bequest to an heir. [Regarding] one who gives the food of another for his own fitr sadaqah, it is contingent upon his permission; if he permits with its conditions and guarantees it, it is valid. The one ordered to pay zakah, if he gives charity from his own dirhams with the intention of reimbursement and the dirhams of the orderer are still in his possession, it suffices. [If] he intended zakah but called it a loan, they differed, and the correct [view] is permissibility. A service slave, if permitted to trade, is not [considered] for trade, so fitr sadaqah is obligatory for him. If the one making a vow specifies a poor person, he may give to another unless he did not specify the vowed [item]; as if he said, 'I owe Allah to feed this poor person something,' then it is specified. If he specifies two poor persons, he may limit to one. The one who refuses to pay zakah is imprisoned, and they differed on taking it from him by force, and the relied-upon [view] is no. The year for zakah is lunar, not solar. All charities are forbidden to Banu Hashim: zakah, its work [wage], 'ushr, expiation, or vowed [charity], except voluntary charity and endowment. If he doubts whether he paid zakah or not, he must pay it, because its time is the lifetime. If he deposits wealth and forgets it, then remembers, zakah is not obligatory unless the depositor is known. Debts owed to people prevent the obligation of zakah except for deferred dower if the husband does not intend to pay it. It is disliked to give a full nisab to a poor person from it unless he is in debt or has dependents; if he distributes it among them, he does not give each a nisab. It is disliked to transfer [zakah] except to a relative or more needy [person], or from dar al-harb to dar al-Islam, or to a student of knowledge, or to ascetics, or if it is an accelerated zakah. The chosen [position] is that it is not permissible to give zakah to people of innovation. Giving it to his married sister: if her husband is poor, it is permissible; if he is wealthy and her dower is less than nisab, likewise; and if the [dower] is equal to nisab, it is not permissible, and with this fatwa is given, and similarly regarding the obligation of sacrifice. The child of zina (illegitimate child) is not established in lineage from the fornicator in anything except testimony, and it is not accepted for the fornicator; and in zakah, it is not permissible for the fornicator to give zakah to the child of zina unless [the child] is from a woman with a known husband, as in Jami' al-Fusulayn. Zakah is obligatory with moderate ability, so it is lifted by the destruction of wealth after the year, while fitr sadaqah is obligatory with possible ability, so if he becomes poor after the day of Eid, it is not lifted. 142 If he spends on his relatives with the intention of zakah, it is permissible unless a court judgment obliged him to support them. Charity is permissible for one who has rental income insufficient for himself and his dependents for a year. One who has a thousand [dirhams] and owes the same, it is disliked for him to take [zakah] but it suffices the payer. If he has sustenance for a year equal to nisab, or winter clothing he does not need in summer, the correct [view] is that it is permissible to take [zakah]. If he accelerates [payment] for a nisab he has, then the year completes while he has less than nisab: if he paid it to the poor person, he does not take it back at all; to the collector, he takes it back if it is still in existence, and if the collector distributed it to the poor, he compensates it from the zakah funds; contrary to Muhammad. If he accelerates the zakah of grazing animals after their birth, it is permissible, not before. And in al-Multaqat min al-Ijarah: If a teacher gives something to his substitute intending zakah, if [the substitute] would work for him even if he did not give it, it is valid as zakah, otherwise not.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a collection of specific rulings (rasm) on various issues related to zakah, as established in the Hanafi madhhab. It begins with the ruling on a terminally ill person paying zakah to an heir: the zakah is valid but if there is another heir, the payment is considered a bequest to an heir (which is invalid) and thus must be returned. Then it discusses cases where one acts on behalf of another, such as giving fitr sadaqah with someone else's food or paying zakah from one's own money with the intention of reimbursement. There is a dispute whether calling a payment 'loan' while intending zakah is valid; the correct view according to the text is permissibility. For a service slave permitted to trade, the permission is not for trade per se, so fitr sadaqah remains obligatory on the owner. Regarding vows, if a person specifies a particular poor person, he may still give to another unless the vowed item itself was specified (e.g., feeding a particular person). If two are specified, he can give to only one. The state can imprison a person who refuses to pay zakah, but taking it by force is not the relied-upon view. The zakah year is lunar. Charities including zakah, 'ushr, kaffara, and vowed charity are forbidden to Banu Hashim, except voluntary charity and endowments. Doubt about payment requires payment because the obligation lasts a lifetime (until death). Forgetting deposited wealth does not trigger zakah unless the depositor is known. Debts owed to people prevent zakah obligation, except deferred dower if the husband does not intend to pay it. Giving a full nisab to one poor person is disliked unless he is in debt or has dependents. Transferring zakah to a different locality is disliked except for relatives, more needy, from war zone to Islamic land, to students or ascetics, or if it is accelerated. Giving to innovators is not permissible. Giving to a married sister depends on her husband's wealth and her dower. An illegitimate child from zina does not inherit but can receive zakah if the mother has a known husband (to avoid suspicion). Zakah is lifted if the wealth is destroyed after the year, but fitr sadaqah is not lifted if one becomes poor after Eid. Spending on relatives with zakah intention is valid unless obligated by court. The criteria for being eligible to receive zakah are detailed: one with insufficient rental income for a year can take; one with equal assets and debts may take but it is disliked; having a year's sustenance equal to nisab does not prevent taking; accelerated payment before year end is valid in certain conditions. Finally, a teacher giving zakah to a substitute is valid only if the substitute would have worked without the gift.

Key Terms
المختار (al-mukhtār): The relied-upon or preferred position in the Hanafi madhhab, as opposed to weaker opinions.
صدقة الفطر (ṣadaqat al-fiṭr): The obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan, also called fitr sadaqah.
حول الزكاة (ḥawal al-zakāh): The lunar year that must pass for zakah to become obligatory on wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it permissible to give zakah to a married sister?
A) Always, if she is poor.
B) Only if her husband is poor.
C) If her husband is poor, or if her husband is wealthy but her dower is less than nisab.
D) It is never permissible because she is a relative.

Key Takeaway
Zakah rulings are highly context-dependent: a mufti must examine the specific circumstances of the giver, recipient, and timing before issuing a fatwa.
